Dismissed with a Laugh 139

— Hai Ke

A: Every time I quarrel with my wife, I have to record it in detail in my notebook. Over the past ten years, it has become quite a collection.

B: Since that's the case, why not publish it? It would be another great work like "All Quiet on the Western Front."

Mother: Every time you go to church to pray, you must pray for each member of the family without forgetting.

Son: I know, but in last week's prayer, I excluded my sister.

Mother: Why did you exclude her?

Son: Because she just got engaged, so the blessing has already been given.

A: The Japanese say "Good morning," and the sound is like "Wah-ha-wah."

B: That's easy to remember, the same as the place name of Wah-ha-wah State in the United States.

A: When I was studying in the United States, I heard such a joke: One Japanese classmate met an American classmate in the morning and said to him as usual, "Wah-ha-wah." The American classmate didn't know what was going on and hurriedly replied, "Mississippi."

Police officer (asking a lost woman holding a baby): Woman, do you have a home? Who is at home?

Woman: There are two other children, this one is just a sample.

Unofficial History of Fishing Boats 140

— Lian Weng

The theory of the nine-surname fishing boats in Zhejiang is that Chen Youliang and his generals belonged to nine surnames in the spring, such as Chen, Cheng, Ye, and Xu. Emperor Taizu of Ming hated Chen and tricked him onto the boat, forbidding him from landing. He showed it to the Tinghu households in Guangdong and the households in Yong, etc. to show his demotion. After the national system was changed, the Zhejiang People's Hall began to discuss abolishing the old rules and ordered the counties where boats were moored to investigate and report separately. Now there are signs of success. From then on, there will be no more sweet-scented osmanthus paddles or orchid-decorated oars coming and going in Qili Longzhong on the Qiantang River.

Fishing boats gather on both sides of the Jianggan Gate, like wild geese with ropes strung together like pearls. The springboards are horizontal and vertical, and they all meander in one breath. The rails of the boats are half-rolled up, and those leaning on the railings are mostly beautiful women. The married women are the wives of those born in the same year, and the unmarried women are the sisters of those born in the same year. This is because most of them are from Tonglu and Yanzhou. Tong and Yan are a sound shift of those born in the same year. The Qing Dynasty had a boat bureau to manage the assets. All officials going upstream drove this boat at full speed, and those passing through were also like this. If they were idle and bored, young men in silk robes and wooden clogs would borrow them as places to set up banquets. At that time, the reputation was extremely important, not just a song and a bundle of silk. During the Qing Dynasty, the bureau was abolished, and the women also moved their boats to the shore, displaying their colorful flags between the Haiyue Bridge and the Huapai Building.

Outside of Jianggan, only the boats of Lanxi and Yandongguan are still considered medium-class. If you go down to Quzhou and Longyou, and reach Yiqiao and Wenyan, although they are the same fishing boats, the furnishings and social gatherings are inferior. The boats turn around and leave. Even if you know Yan Ge well, you don't easily enter his tent. Otherwise, the turbans you want to get will cost thousands of dollars. Attendant Lang Zhupo fell in love with a woman and actually hired her for five thousand gold and impeached himself and resigned. The so-called imperial clan, the Eight Banners, famous scholars, grass, Jiangshan, nine-surname beauty, and hemp. The fishing boat is also called Jiangshan boat, so there is this couplet. Although there have been slight changes recently, the scholars did not dare to ask for the tripod. Once it is eliminated and restored to freedom, its merits will be ten times better than Jiliang's.

Alas, I can't forget Pupu's pipa and Bai Chuan's strings and songs in Qinhuai. I hate people and keep my old Hongxue. When I get this news, I dance and squat. I take notes with tears. I just keep the old stories of the southern fireworks.

Ancient Customs of Sichuan 141

— Zhi Zheng

Dai Jitao, President of the Examination Yuan, said in a speech one day that Sichuan Province is rich in ancient customs, because the residents do not close their doors at night, do not pick up lost items on the road, the sounds of chickens and dogs are not heard, and the people do not interact with each other until they die. At that time, the listeners all praised him. However, Mr. Dai is from Sichuan and almost suspected that he was exaggerating his words. Then Mr. Dai explained, "Those who do not close their doors at night are because the houses of the people have been turned into ruins and broken walls by the artillery fire after the war, and there are no doors to close. Those who do not pick up lost items on the road are because they have been digging up tree roots and grass skin to eat due to years of famine, and there is nothing to pick up. The chickens and dogs have all been slaughtered, so what sounds can be heard? The people have been displaced and scattered, so even if they want to interact with each other, they cannot say they have. Sighs are endless." Therefore, those who sighed that the ancient customs of Sichuan still exist could not help but feel depressed, and on the other hand, they admired Mr. Dai's skill in speaking.

In Memory of Yu Shuyan 142

— Xu Xiaoting

Among those who perform male roles with beards in Peking opera, two stand out for their ability to assimilate the strengths of others and make them their own through ingenuity: Tan Xinpei and Yu Shuyan. Old Tan, due to his local connections, was initially closer to Yu Sansheng. He also favored using clever techniques to achieve flexibility and beauty in his melodies, rather than relying on brute force. This aligned with Yu Sansheng's approach, so his art was heavily influenced by Yu, while also drawing from Cheng and Wang, selecting the best and expanding upon it to create the Tan school. Shuyan, as the grandson of Yu Sansheng and the son of Ziyun, had a distinguished family background. Later, he studied with Old Tan, gathering the essence of Yu Sansheng and Xinpei, combined with his own inherent strengths, to create his personal art, thus establishing the Yu school. It can be compared to a businessman: Old Tan initially borrowed capital from Yu Sansheng, widely adopted the strengths of others, and, like adding his own funds, greatly profited. Later, when Shuyan sought to reclaim his original capital, Old Tan provided him with as much as he could, including Yu Sansheng's original artistry, supplemented with the learning of Cheng and Wang, repaying the principal with interest. Thus, Shuyan received significant assistance. He also relied on his family's legacy as a foundation and knew how to utilize his own ingenuity to pioneer new paths. Therefore, although his achievements did not break free from the Tan school's framework, his timing was particularly fortunate. Unlike Old Tan, who faced strong rivals like Wang and Sun, he was able to firmly establish his dominance. Hence, the name of the Yu school was established not long ago, and it has already been admired both North and South. Shuyan achieved seventy to eighty percent of Old Tan's art. However, due to his relatively lesser talent, he often modified what he felt unable to master, revealing weaknesses. Some used this to attack him for not adhering to Tan's methods, denouncing him as a "false Tan." In reality, Shuyan had his own irreplaceable qualities, and it's inappropriate to belittle him for this. Shuyan had unique insights regarding the use of falsetto, making it as resonant and melodious as his natural voice. He was meticulous in his study of the four tones and the distinction between palatal and retroflex initials. However, his use of abrupt sounds was excessive, and the endings of his phrases often felt too rushed. His martial arts skills were due to his early performance of martial plays such as "Picking the Hua Che" and "The Linked Rings," demonstrating steady and precise movements. Few can match him today. Watching his Kunqu opera "Ning Wu Pass" and the Peking opera "The Battle of Taiping" reveals the depth of his skill. Furthermore, his "Washing Floating Mountain" and "He Tianbao" demonstrated skills in tossing horses and wielding knives, skills that can only be accomplished with genuine ability. Aside from Shuyan, Yang Baosen also devoted himself to this play. Shuyan excelled in spoken drama. Watching his short play "Losing the Seal and Rescuing from Fire" is far superior to the current popular plays such as "Borrowing the East Wind" and "The Honest Official's Record." However, today's audiences seem to treat theater like a buffet: they only crave quantity and don't have time to appreciate the flavor. It's no wonder they favor lengthy and strenuous plays like "Borrowing the East Wind." Shuyan was not only skilled in acting but also excelled in playing the jinghu. His jinghu player, Li Peiqing, was often personally instructed by Shuyan in composing and adjusting melodies, resulting in a lively and dynamic quality. Experts have often stated that a good singer must also be skilled in playing the jinghu. Today, few performers can fulfill this criterion. Moreover, Shuyan possessed both civil and martial skills, and was proficient in Kunqu opera. Who else can compare to him? Shuyan was literate and skilled in calligraphy. The plaque of the Peking Opera Guild of Beiping bears his elegant writing, a rare achievement for a performer today. It has been seven years since Shanghai last saw Shuyan's performance. I and my friends Shaoqing eagerly await his early arrival in the South to dispel the demonic atmosphere of pretentious and trendy male actors.

A Theatergoer's Notes on Tiansheng Theater 143

— Lao Zhuo

Xue Yanqin has come to Shanghai for the second time. I had never seen her before, but those who have always praise her beauty. Recently, I and my friends have been watching plays at Tiansheng Theater every night, and I have seen her perform in "Lian Jin Feng," "Pan Si Dong," and "June Snow." All of them are excellent. Her costumes are delicate and beautiful, her figure is slender and well-proportioned, her recitations are clear, and her singing voice is round and melodious. She is especially good at using her voice to create light and agile transitions that are captivating. With all these qualities, it is no wonder that she is highly praised. She is indeed a top female performer. I also watched Hao Shuchen perform "Zhan Ma Su" and "Xie Ma Su," which depicted Ma Su's stubbornness; and "Da Cao Bao," which depicted General Cao Bao's drunkenness and recklessness. His "Peach Blossom Village" depicted Lu Zhishen's boorishness and his habit of fighting for justice. The expressions were all lifelike, and his spoken lines were as forceful as cutting nails. He is unmatched among contemporary clowns. I have greatly enjoyed watching these plays, so I am writing this record.

Brief News: The Yage Society, which has been established for twenty-one years, was once a prominent organization in Shanghai. The special issues it has published contain works by contemporary celebrities and famous performers, and are widely circulated. The twenty-first anniversary will be celebrated on the eighth and ninth of this month at the Ningbo Fellow-Provincials Association. There will be commemorative performances, and the remaining special issues will also be distributed to the guests. The program is briefly recorded as follows: (Daytime performances on the eighth) "Yuejia Village," "Wulong Yuan," "Meilong Zhen," "Li Ling Stele," "June Snow," "Beating the Dragon Robe," "The Pearl Curtain Village" (Evening performances on the eighth) "Luoma Lake," "Sitting in the Tower and Killing the Daughter-in-Law," "Farewell to the Kiln," "The Flower Chronicle," "Cui Ping Mountain," "Fen River Bay," "The Golden Horse Gate," "Slaying the Sutras" (Evening performances on the ninth) "Double Shaking Society," "Double Song Jiang," "Double Lions Picture," "Double Dragon Society," "Double Utmost Loyalty," "Double Golden Lotus," "Double Bao Case," "Double Heavenly Master"

Introduction to Publications: The "Zhengqi" daily newspaper, sponsored by the Plum Blossom Hall, has been published for five months. Yesterday, the "Fiftieth Issue Commemorative Special" was released, with inscriptions by famous figures such as Sun Zhesheng, Beiwu Shanren, Tan Pingzhai, Pan Gongzhan, You Bankuang, and Huang Zhuan Tao. The illustrations include a wedding photo of Mr. and Mrs. Cai Yuanpei, and glamorous photos of the four elders of the courtesan world: Yang Lanchun, Tanchun, and Cuifang. The content is rich. Newspapers are distributed by all news vendors. For out-of-town subscriptions, please contact the newspaper office at No. 976, Yuren Lane, Yunnan Road, Shanghai.

Impressions of West Lake (Part 1) 144

— Huijian

I have been living in the human sea of Beijing for six years, and I have been engaged in the life of a scribe, my body and mind are exhausted. One day, I gathered with my companions at the Qinhuai River. In the boat, someone suggested traveling for two or three days. Some proposed going to Louxia Mountain to see the red leaves, while others proposed going to Tangshan for an autumn bath. However, they are not far from Beijing, only enough for a half-day round trip, and the taste is not strong. Everyone was hesitant. Suddenly, someone quietly rose and said, "The refreshing breeze and flowing water of West Lake have been lingering in my mind for a long time. If you are willing to join me, I will depart on the morning train tomorrow. Please make a decision quickly." I happily agreed first, and Si Lan also applauded in approval.

On October 5th, the three of us went to Shanghai by morning train and stayed in a hotel for one night. On the morning of the 6th, we changed to a bus to Hangzhou. In the bus, we further discussed going to Haining to watch the tide on the 8th. Traveling from Hangzhou by the highway bureau's bus is convenient because the road is not very long and the cost is also lower, compared to taking a special train from the Shanghai-Hangzhou railway. We arrived in Hangzhou at around 2 PM and got two rooms in a hotel by the lake. This day was the Mid-Autumn Festival in the old calendar, and there were many people watching the tide who had come to West Lake in advance. The commercial districts by the lake were very lively. After taking a bath in the hotel, we changed into light clothes, took our walking sticks and cameras, and set off. We found a boat near the park pier. Xia Han and the boatman bargained over the price. I quietly stood by the water, revisiting old memories. The entire lake was bathed in the autumn sun, revealing a silver-gray color. A gentle breeze stirred it, revealing golden ripples. The mountains of Longmen on the shore sat majestically, like smiling teeth welcoming visitors. The two high peaks in the north and south still looked menacing as before. Closer up, the Su Causeway was like a belt, lined with verdant willows, an incomparably serene and beautiful scene. The islet of Gushan in the north, with its multiple pavilions and towers, seemed even more magnificent than before. Boats in the lake came and went like shuttles. After we settled the price, we boarded the boat and headed north. We passed a villa, with a graceful blend of Chinese and Western styles. The boatman said it was Zhang Jingjiang's residence, while Xia Han said it was the Hangzhou municipal government. Passing this, we arrived at the Zhaoging Temple pier and went ashore. We saw the colorful temple gate in the distance, seemingly showing its solemnity. Entering the temple to the west wing, we saw a group of monks entering a large room in a line, presumably for dinner. A monk was supervising from the side, his eyes glaring and his nose flared, as if he was very powerful. The monks were afraid and each received a bowl of light yellow vegetables to eat, seeming to enjoy it. We then went to the front hall to visit and saw four or five monks eating at another table. The dishes included five bowls, one being mushrooms and another dried lily flowers in soy sauce. The supervising monk was also sitting among them, eating heartily, and seeming embarrassed to be seen. Leaving the Zhaoging Temple, we proceeded west along the shore to Broken Bridge, where the boatman had already moored the boat to wait. The road here was very well maintained and clean, and there were more Western-style buildings. I heard that land prices on the north shore of West Lake are several times higher than on the south shore. There seems to be a trend at play here.

Warmth in My Heart (310) 145

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 15: Tears Fall in All Directions, Lamenting Red Passions; Hearts are Won, Lingering Green Sentiments

Not long after, Yixing Shu's illness ultimately took its toll. During his illness, he told his friends that he deeply regretted getting married, as it only caused his wife the most pain. Naturally, his wife was the one who suffered the most. The reporter will not continue with this tragic story, as it would only cause grief. At that time, the Pingbao Newspaper had a club called Shanglu, where many friends would often gather during their free time, just like swallows on a beam, coming and going freely. However, among the friends, there were always new faces replacing the old. Some of the regular friends suddenly had other matters and stopped coming, while a new group of friends came instead. Only Long Ziyun, Ling Zhixiang, Yi Yunshang, and Lin Fanzi were regulars who never went anywhere else. They would sometimes patronize male prostitutes and sometimes play small games of mahjong. This was because the newspaper work started in the afternoon at four or five o'clock, and after going to work at seven or eight o'clock, they would take a break to go out for dinner and relax. They would then go back to work at ten o'clock, just like people who work during the day take a lunch break. One day, Long Ziyun invited some friends to a Beijing cuisine restaurant for dinner. Those present were all regulars at the Pingbao Newspaper. The poet Zuo was also among them. Both Ling Zhixiang and Long Ziyun liked to call for prostitutes to sing. They said that without women present, the atmosphere would be dull and uninteresting, causing a sense of dryness. Even if they engaged in leisurely conversation, these people, who met often, had exhausted their topics of conversation. Furthermore, with women present, the atmosphere would often be lively and interesting. Ling Zhixiang then suggested calling for prostitutes. Due to his business relationships, he had many social engagements outside, so he was a prominent figure in the prostitution world. Everyone in the brothels knew him. He was also very easy to talk to. If someone asked him to go to another brothel, he would go. If someone else asked him to go, he would also agree readily. He would sit with someone he recognized, or someone he recognized as a procurer. Over time, he would open dozens of accounts for each festival. Whenever he went out for pleasure, in addition to the people he usually called, he would also let his friends write down names for him, and he would agree casually. Sometimes, when a prostitute came, he wouldn't even know her name or where she lived. He would sit down briefly, say a few words, and leave before the seat was even warm. If you asked him, he wouldn't know either. However, there were some girls with good memories who would engrave the names of the customers who had called them in their hearts, remembering exactly who had been to which brothel. Those who were not good at remembering might have called him three or four times already, but when they called him again a week later, it would be as if they were strangers. This was partly due to memory and partly due to whether they had feelings for that person. Often, in a sea of people, there would be someone with whom you felt an instant connection. It's the same with making friends, like watching flowers and drinking wine while traveling in the northern pleasure quarters.

The editor is urgently making corrections.

The Yarn Market Presents a Situation of Circling Downward 151

The cotton yarn market still appears weak. Standard yarn has fallen three or four taels in recent days, breaking through the 45-tael mark. This is because the actual sales of standard yarn are sluggish, and the various firms are becoming less interested in buying standard yarn due to its weakness, resulting in this downward trend. This is a problem inherent to the yarn market itself, rather than a speculative phenomenon. However, the excessive weakness of the market is enough to trigger a rebound. Moreover, the low price of 144 or 145 taels is already an expected sign. But the sluggish spot sales and the continued decline of Five Blessings and Shepherd brand yarns are obstacles to the development of standard yarn. Even if speculators manage to present a modest improvement, if these adverse obstacles are not removed, the future will still present a situation of circling downward.

Standard yarn fell in the morning and rose at noon. The exchange was bustling with people. Standard yarn opened in the morning with American cotton showing a falling trend, and the sentiment was particularly weak. The Cotton Market Still Lacks a Significant Improvement 152

The cotton market remains weak and sluggish. Inland, the listing of new goods is scarce, and market prices are high, so the sentiment is quite stable. However, the falling trend of foreign cotton has resumed, and factory demand is stagnant, while the yarn market has resumed its downward spiral, and the market sentiment has also become weak. The cotton market itself has no signs of weakness. The current situation relies entirely on the American and Indian cotton markets. The situation in the American cotton market is of particular concern to everyone. American cotton broke through the one-cent barrier due to reduced consumption and low general prices. Later, with the activities of cooperatives, it returned to over one cent and two cents. Recently, with increased production forecasts and no increase in consumption prospects, and the financial turmoil remaining unchanged, the market has weakened again and is showing a falling trend. In terms of the current situation, the key to the American cotton market lies in consumption and financial conditions. The production of 14.5 million bales is unlikely to undergo significant changes, and it is difficult to predict that consumption in the current quarter will exceed that of the previous quarter. Even looking at the weekly statistics of American cotton, the amount of American cotton shipped to factories worldwide in the three months of this quarter was 1,542,000 bales, a huge decrease of 3,310,000 bales compared to the same period last quarter. Even in the United States, it is a decrease of 1 million bales compared to the previous quarter. Under these circumstances, although the government is making efforts to provide relief, its effectiveness is limited. Therefore, the fundamental problem of American cotton lies in consumption. If consumption still does not see any special development in the next two or three months, and the financial situation remains unstable, the cotton market may see new low prices again. The government, on the one hand, is stockpiling, and on the other hand, is advising cotton farmers to reduce the acreage of new cotton fields next season. However, in comparison with the prices of general agricultural products in the United States, it is difficult to say what crops are suitable for planting. Recalling that the Bureau of Agriculture also advised farmers to reduce cotton planting acreage in the spring, but the result was what it was. Therefore, the effect of the movement to reduce cotton planting cannot but be doubted. With the situation of American cotton being what it is, it is difficult to expect the trend of the Indian cotton market to develop. If native cotton relies on American and Indian cotton in this way, then the general trend can be roughly understood. Hankou standard cotton follows the yarn market and stabilizes. In the morning, the Hankou standard cotton market saw a decline of over 20 pounds in American cotton and a weak yarn market. Japanese merchants were aggressively selling, and the market sentiment was extremely weak. Prices for all months fell by 2.5 to 3 cents. In the afternoon, with demand remaining stagnant, the market remained soft. Later, as the yarn market rebounded strongly, the market plate also tightened. Near-month contracts rebounded by 5 cents to 1 cent, while far-month contracts remained flat and weak. The total trading volume was 85,900 piculs. As a result, this month was better by 2 li and a half compared to the previous day, January was smaller by 1 fen 2 li and a half, February was smaller by 7 li and a half, and the rest were unchanged. The entire city only offered slightly over 1,000 packages of Yaowan wheat, with secondary offerings being slightly higher by 1 qian or 2 qian, handled by Fufeng.

Raw Silk and Tea Shanghai White Factory Price Outlook Increasingly Weak 160

Yesterday, the Shanghai foreign firm silk market's price for Shanghai white raw silk factory was increasingly weak. The reason was that silk sales in the European and American markets were not picking up, and the trend of Yokohama's Japanese silk was not improving. Telegrams from Europe to Shanghai were scarce. Yesterday, only Renna imported ten packages of spot goods, and the Shanghai factory price had already fallen to 800 taels. Xinfu imported eight packages of Sichuan reeling silk, and the price was also flat and weak.

Twenty Pieces of Wuxi White Raw Silk Factory Goods Arrive 161

Since the Shanghai silk factories affiliated with Shanghai's silk factories went on strike, because some shareholders entrusted silk orders and the work was relatively busy, twenty pieces of white raw silk from Zhenyi Silk Factory, Jin Shuangying and other brands were transported by the Shanghai-Wuxi passenger train yesterday, to make up for the orders for the previous month that had not been resolved.

Qimen Black Tea Russian Sales Continue to Be Smooth 162

Yesterday, in the Shanghai foreign firm tea market, the Russian Assistance Association's import interest in Qimen black tea continued to be strong. Over 1,000 boxes were transacted throughout the city, and the trading was not sluggish. However, the opening price was impossible to increase due to the small sales of British firms' shopkeepers. Luzhuang Zhenmei pearl tea, Tongfu Jinlong, and other shops all moved to buy Tunxi core-extracted goods. The top-quality price was set at 160 taels, and ordinary Zhenmei was priced at 85 taels, with no increase or decrease compared to last week. However, based on the current market situation, it is still difficult for the market to stabilize.

Sugar Market: Coarse Sugar and White Sugar Gradually Trend Lower 163

New York Sugar Rebounds Strongly

Yesterday, the sugar market reported that the price of Cuban spot sugar remained at 1.4375, the price of New York sugar futures for December was 1.38, March next year was 1.46, down 5 points from the previous telegram, May was 1.52, down 4 points, and September was 1.65, also down 6 points. The price of Java spot sugar was 8.1275, and the price of futures sugar for November and December was both 8.125, with no increase or decrease. The exchange market divided and planned Dutch sugar 24. The buying interest in coarse sugar white was still scarce. The initial price was 7 taels and 8 qian and a half. Demand was scarce. Later, some transactions were made at 7 taels and 8 qian. The market was still weak and lacked spirit. Ground fine sugar white was 7 taels and 8 qian and a half, and 20-count medium sugar white was 6 taels and 9 qian. Inquiries were also rare. Although transactions of Japanese sugar were scarce, the market shape was slightly flat. N Mark 7 taels 7 qian and a half, J Mark 8 taels 05 fen, SH Mark 7 taels 4 qian and a half, New Goods 7 taels 5 qian, TR Mark 7 taels 9 qian 2 fen and a half, YT Mark 7 taels 6 qian 3 fen 7 li and a half to 7 taels 6 qian and a half, YR〇 Mark 7 taels 3 qian 2 fen and a half. The trend is still firm. The dumping intentions of Dutch sugar merchants are very weak, and only Yuanji and Xiangmao foreign firms are selling, with each selling 200-300 tons. The trend is likely to show a gradual decline.

Banking Sector

Regulations for New Year Holidays 184

Four Days of Closure for New Year's Day

Two Days of Closure for Spring Festival

According to sources in the banking sector, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and various banking associations have already agreed to follow the National Government's decree to abolish the lunar calendar. The 17th and 18th of February are set as the Spring Festival holidays for two days of closure. In addition, January 1st to 3rd will be New Year's holidays. Together with Sunday, the 4th, there will be a total of four days of closure. For the sake of coordination, foreign banks have also decided to follow this regulation for both the Gregorian calendar and the abolished lunar calendar New Year holidays to facilitate operations.

Economic Aggression by Japanese Businesses 192

To Avoid Heavy Taxes from the New Tariff

Many Plan to Establish Factories in Shanghai and Qingdao

A Tokyo dispatch from the China Mail states: "Since the implementation of China's autonomous tariff and the new tariff rules, many Japanese exporters are planning to establish factories in Shanghai and Qingdao to avoid heavy taxes and compete with Chinese factories. It is heard that the Takegawa Rubber Company, in view of the profits made by Sakata Company in manufacturing rubber galoshes in Shanghai, will soon open a branch factory in China. The aluminum ware manufacturing industry also plans to do the same, and to avoid competition among themselves, the larger manufacturers will jointly establish a factory. Its products will first be sold in China, and any surplus will be shipped to other places. Other industries will also follow suit to invade the Chinese market. The Japanese textile industry plans to expand existing factories in China because Chinese labor is cheap and silver is valuable, making it possible to operate in China. It is expected that the Chinese government will increase import duties on cotton textiles to protect its nascent industries. Manufacturing in China can avoid heavy taxes. Furthermore, China not only has low labor costs, but also reduces costs by allowing night work for twenty-two or twenty-four hours. Therefore, the Japanese textile industry advocates greatly expanding existing factories in China and uniting to become the vanguard of market invasion."

American Initiative for International Travel Exposition 193

Ministry of Transportation Notifies the Aviation Industry

Soliciting Achievements of Road and Air Transportation

The Ministry of Transportation, due to the American steamship company Travel Agency's initiative for an international travel exposition, is soliciting achievements from China's aviation industry for display at the exhibition hall in the United States. The exhibition period is set for February 9th to 14th next year, to be held at the Grand Central Palace in New York. It has been agreed to invite representatives from railway, steamship, and other companies from various countries to attend the meeting. Aside from already consulting with the Ministry of Railways for consideration, the rules of the exposition are hereby copied and sent to the Shanghai shipping industry for prompt discussion and response. Those with achievements or who wish to participate should report to the ministry for consideration. The explanatory brochure for the exhibition hall is recorded below:

"Dates": From February 9th to 14th, 1931. "Location": Grand Central Palace, New York City. This palace is the most magnificent and famous exhibition venue in the United States, located in the heart of New York City, accessible to a metropolitan area with twelve to fifteen million residents, the wealthiest market in the world. "Purpose": To highlight excellent travel opportunities, stimulate public interest in travel, promote the joint development of the travel industry, make them aware of the economy, comfort, and variety of modern travel, widely promote the work of foreign travel entrepreneurs in contacting American businesses, and publicize the scenery, culture, and commercial interests of various countries to enhance international understanding and harmony. "Value of the Exposition": It is estimated that the number of visitors to this exhibition will be around one hundred thousand, mostly people with a strong interest in travel. Therefore, anything displayed will undoubtedly leave a deep impression on them, which can be guaranteed. Coupled with simultaneous publicity through newspapers, radio, and film, it will undoubtedly spread opinions and suggestions on travel to millions of people both at home and abroad. "Exhibition Hall Facilities": This international travel exposition will not only display the achievements of various countries' railways, steamships, and aviation (such as travel maps, etc.), but also feature various performances and dances from different countries, as well as music, songs, and lectures by famous explorers every afternoon and evening to arouse special interest in travel among the audience. "Exhibition Hall Rental Fees": The fees to be paid by participants will depend on the area occupied by the exhibits and the type of items. Calculated by area, each square foot requires three US dollars. The sizes of the booths vary, with the smallest being ten feet square, requiring three hundred US dollars, and the largest being twenty-nine feet wide and twenty-two feet long, requiring one thousand nine hundred and fourteen US dollars. If there are special arrangements, there will be additional charges, the amount of which will depend on the complexity of the arrangements.

Government's Major Disaster Relief Plan 197

Chairman Xu Shiying of the Relief Committee has two types of plans for disaster relief: short-term and long-term. The short-term plan involves requesting the government to allocate relief funds and for the committee to raise funds to aid various provinces affected by disasters, which is a temporary emergency measure.

The long-term plan is a permanent and comprehensive plan submitted by the Executive Yuan to the National Government and then sent to the Legislative Yuan for revision and approval, known as the Disaster Relief Reserve Fund Law. It has been promulgated by the National Government. The articles are recorded below:

Article 1: The National Government shall allocate one percent of the total regular budget revenue each year as the central disaster relief reserve fund, but it may be stopped after the accumulation of 50 million yuan.

Article 2: The provincial government shall allocate two percent of the total regular budget revenue each year as the provincial disaster relief reserve fund. The provincial disaster relief reserve fund shall be based on population, and may be stopped after the accumulation of 200,000 yuan for every million people. The aforementioned budget expenditure.

Article 3: A management committee shall be established for the disaster relief reserve fund. At the central level, it shall be organized by seven members appointed by the National Government, with the Minister of Interior and the Minister of Finance as ex officio members. At the provincial level, the committee shall be organized by five members appointed by the Executive Yuan upon request of the provincial government, with the Director of Civil Affairs and the Director of Finance as ex officio members. The central disaster relief reserve fund management committee shall be supervised by the Executive Yuan, and the provincial disaster relief reserve fund management committee shall be supervised by the provincial government in handling its affairs.

Article 4: The expenses of the management committee shall not be drawn from the disaster relief reserve fund.

Article 5: The disaster relief reserve fund shall be the responsibility of the management committee and shall not be used for other purposes.

Article 6: In the event of a disaster that cannot be handled by the city or county, the provincial disaster relief reserve fund shall be used for subsidies. If it is insufficient, the central disaster relief reserve fund shall be used for subsidies. Work relief or immigration related to disaster relief may be subsidized from the disaster relief reserve fund. The amount of subsidy for the preceding two items shall be decided by the management committee and submitted to the supervisory authority for approval.

Article 7: The disaster relief reserve fund shall be properly deposited in national banks or reliable banks and shall accrue interest on a regular basis. The aforementioned deposits shall have priority in being cleared.

Article 8: If the disaster relief reserve fund suffers losses due to the negligence of the custodian, the custodian shall be liable for compensation.

Article 9: If the interest generated by the disaster relief reserve fund in the current year is insufficient to pay due to the disaster situation, the disaster relief reserve fund may be used, but not exceeding one-half of the existing amount.

Article 10: The management committee shall prepare annual budgets and final accounts for the income, expenditure, and custody of the disaster relief reserve fund and report them to the supervisory authority separately.

Article 11: This law shall come into effect from the date of promulgation.

Disaster Reports from Minquan and Taikang Counties Received by the Red Cross 198

The Shanghai Red Cross Society received a telegram yesterday from the Henan Provincial Relief Committee, forwarded from the Minquan County Magistrate reporting the disaster situation. The telegram reads:

"To the China Red Cross Society,

According to the report from Liu Guanzhong, the magistrate of Minquan County, the county has been in a war zone for a long time, resulting in particularly severe losses. From April to September, it was lost and recovered five times. Subsequent investigations reveal more than 330 casualties, the loss of over 1,250 large carts, more than 3,230 head of livestock, over 2,300 acres of crops trampled, over 7,200 acres of trenches dug, over 679,000 catties of grain requisitioned, over 1,830,000 catties of firewood and straw requisitioned, and other trees, beams, pillars, wooden boards, doors, and windows looted, the value of which is incalculable. At present, the war has ended, and the fields are desolate. The hungry and cold are isolated and helpless, pleading for immediate relief. Minquan is a key point on the Longhai Railway, the focus of the war, with smoke and fire filling the sky, villages turned into ruins, and fields into ravines. Corpses are everywhere, and the miserable conditions of the displaced are unbearable to witness. We earnestly pray for advance rescue and generous aid so that the survivors can preserve their lives. We are anxiously awaiting your response.

Zhang Fang of the Henan Relief Committee, bowing in winter."

Another telegram was received from the Taikang County Relief Sub-Committee, briefly stating: "Repeatedly ravaged by local bandits Liu Laosan and Zhang Fengzi, the people cannot bear their fate. By the turn of summer and autumn, rebel armies gathered, numbering over 200,000, extending from Longqu in the north to Laozhong in the south, and from Changying in the west to Zhukou in the east, covering dozens of villages and hundreds of square miles. Each household was stationed with military camps. The old and young alike were forced into service. Trenches crisscrossed, and farmland was damaged. Carts and horses were requisitioned, and farmers were unable to farm. When the national army advanced, the rebel army resisted fiercely. Airplanes soared in the sky, and bombs exploded on the ground. Although people wanted to escape, there was no way to heaven and no way to burrow into the earth. Unexpectedly, villages became targets for artillery fire, and houses became targets for airplanes. With a deafening crash, several zhang of red smoke arose, and houses were reduced to ashes. People were turned into minced meat. Such tragic scenes are common in areas close to the front lines. Those families who were fortunate enough not to be hit by bombs still had their food, clothing, and livestock looted by the rebel army, leaving nothing behind. Even chickens, dogs, sheep, and pigs were slaughtered, and there were no remaining pieces of furniture or utensils to be used as fuel. Nevertheless, they still forcibly levied donations of over 200,000 yuan, requisitioned over 30 million catties of wheat, and requisitioned bran and firewood accordingly, conscripting four to five thousand soldiers and over ten thousand laborers. Those who escaped death from bombs will inevitably succumb to freezing and starvation. The continuous war has lasted for seven months. At the time of the rebel army's collapse, banditry spread everywhere, and the misery of arson and slaughter was unprecedented. Today, all that is seen are red walls standing, rubble piled up, the smell of blood but no smoke from cooking. The disaster victims are anxious and miserable, with suffering too difficult to bear, eating in the wind and sleeping in the dew, and with whom can their grievances be told? Their mournful cries shake the sky, and they are crying out for food, waiting for relief.

The Red Cross has repeatedly received disaster reports from various parts of Henan Province and is actively raising funds to prepare for winter relief."

Dissolution of the Pacific Freight Alliance 199

Various shipping companies traveling on the Pacific route, due to the high value of gold and the low value of silver, and the soaring freight rates, but also due to the small amount of cargo and intense competition, organized the Pacific Freight Alliance in this city in mid-July. After a few months of trial operation, due to operational reasons and mutual misunderstanding, it has been decided to dissolve the alliance after the trial period has ended.

The Baihe River is Open, Blocking Ships: This year, the Baihe River waterway opened earlier. A few days ago, a hurricane caused twenty-six or seven ships bound for Tianjin to be blocked at the Dagukou and unable to enter. Passengers and cargo were transferred to small boats. Yesterday, news from Tianjin stated that the commercial ships stopped at Tanggu had resumed sailing successively because the wind had stopped. However, it was no longer possible for ships with deeper drafts to enter Zizhu Forest, so passengers disembarked in Tanggu.

The Tianjin Maru suffered serious damage to its hull and has been suspended from service for repairs. The cost of repairs is estimated to be about 10,000 taels. It will resume sailing to Shanghai after the repairs are completed.

Overview of the Business Operations of the Upper Yangtze Shipping Company's Vessels in the Middle and Lower Yangtze River 201

Chinese and Foreign Aviation Compete with Each Other

This year, the Yangtze River shipping industry has been affected by the current situation, and imports and exports have been sluggish. Recently, due to the accumulation of goods in Jiangxi Province, cargo is being shipped downstream from the upper reaches in large quantities. The various steamships in Shanghai have been competing fiercely for business on the Yangtze River. What I know is recorded as follows:

Taikoo Company: The British Taikoo Company has the most ships and the largest tonnage in the Yangtze River. It has always been the leader among the six companies in terms of upstream and downstream business. This year, the company's Yangtze River business is not as good as before, with a particular shortage of local goods. Fortunately, there are more transshipment goods from the South and North Oceans. However, it has retreated behind Japanese ships in terms of business. It is said that since February, income and expenditure have not been able to offset each other. Fortunately, the accumulated profits are huge, and there is no loss. The company's focus has shifted to the upper reaches, starting with extending the routes of Anqing, Datong, and Poyang ships to Yichang. Then, new oil-powered ships were added, specializing in the Shanghai-Yichang route. At the same time, the upstream shipping rates were reduced, and business improved slightly. On the upstream route, the number of cargo pieces on the Hankou route is not as good as the number of cargo pieces on the Yichang route, with each ship exporting only three to four thousand pieces on average.

Nisshin Kisen Kaisha: The Nisshin Kisen Kaisha originally specialized in coal routes. After increasing the number of ships on the North and South Oceans and foreign seas, the amount of transshipment cargo has also increased significantly. This year, all the Yangtze River vessels are in decline, but the export cargo of this company can still maintain sixty to seventy percent. The most profitable cargo, yarn cloth, accounts for the largest share among the six companies. Recently, it has even begun to seize the cigarette transport business that Jardine Matheson exclusively handles, so the cargo on each ship is often more than on other ships. It is very accommodating to the brokers, giving rebates and gifts. As a result, its business is better than other companies. Currently, there are six Yangtze River vessels per week and one Yichang vessel every other day. Because the upper reaches can be loaded, large quantities of rapeseed, wheat bran, cotton seed, and other goods are being transported to the East from Hubei, Jiangxi, and Anhui. The Yangtze River imports and exports of this company have already jumped to first place this year.

Jardine Matheson: Jardine Matheson's Yangtze River vessels are also very sluggish this year. However, the Yichang vessel once a week still has good cargo, so the newly built ship, Shihe, can start sailing this month. Recently, export cargo is not as good as downstream cargo, with only five sailings per week. The exclusive transport of cash and large quantities of kerosene belongs to this company. The Mingsheng, a "wild chicken" vessel on the Yangtze River route, has already been sold.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company: China Merchants' Yangtze River business has been severely hit this year due to too many vessel suspensions and schedule disruptions. However, vessels can be gradually returned to service this week, and the regular schedule is expected to resume from next week. Recently, the company's export cargo has seen a sudden increase. The cargo of large ships on the one-four schedule has always been around 10,000 taels. Even the Jiangyu, a small ship that sailed yesterday, received more than 7,000 taels. Now it is just beginning to reorganize. If it can fully recover, it should be able to surpass the British and Japanese vessels. The company has exclusive transport rights to Datong, Anqing, and other ports, and foreign vessels cannot compete.

San Peh Steam Navigation Company: San Peh's Yangtze River vessels were also suspended this year. This month, vessels such as Xinning, Xingguang, Hongyuan, and Hongheng have started sailing. The newly built 700-ton Hong-class vessel will also be able to start sailing soon. Recently, because the accumulated cargo in Shashi and Jiujiang in the upper reaches has begun to be loaded in Shanghai, the company specially ordered the iron barges in the upper Yangtze to carry downstream cargo to Shanghai and Hankou because of the insufficient number of vessels.

Ning Shao and Zhaoxing: The Ning Shao Company is still dispatching the old Ning Shao vessel. The newly purchased Ning Jing vessel is currently chartered out and cannot be dispatched for the time being. The Zhaoxing Company's Yangtze River vessels are currently the Zhaoxing and Rongxing vessels. However, they only dock at Wuhu and Xunyang along the way, so the cargo loaded is only sugar and iron. There is no transshipment business, so it seems difficult to compete with other companies.

Jiejiang Xiangtai: The Jiejiang Company is a US-owned company that specializes in the upper reaches. It currently has four Shanghai-Yichang vessels and four Chongqing vessels. The export business is still considered good, with about 60% cargo per sailing. However, recently, the freight rates in the upper reaches have been affected by the drastic price cuts of British and Japanese vessels. The Xiangtai vessel is a British vessel that initially specialized in transporting its own timber, but now it also transports passengers and cargo. There are a total of two vessels in service. In total, the nine Yangtze River companies have eighty-seven vessels on the upstream and downstream routes.

Membership Withdrawal from Trade Associations 205

Approved by the Ministry: Pass by the Executive Committee First

Then Submitted to the General Assembly for Retroactive Approval

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to various industry trade associations yesterday, stating:

"Regarding the case where the Shanghai Silk Trade Association previously stated that Article 7 of the trade association's constitution stipulated, 'Members who wish to withdraw from the association must submit a written statement stating the reasons, which must be approved by a majority vote of the general membership before they can withdraw.' They believed that the general membership meeting was held once a year, and members requesting withdrawal was a common occurrence, making it difficult to handle according to the regulations. Therefore, they proposed a flexible approach: first, the executive committee would resolve the matter, and then the new member would be retroactively approved, and the matter would be reported for review.

The Chamber of Commerce believed that this restriction was a provision of the association's constitution, and there was no explicit provision in the Trade Association Law and its implementation rules. The flexible approach proposed by the trade association could be resolved by amending Article 7 of the association's constitution at the next general membership meeting. However, before Article 7 of the constitution has been resolved and amended, could the flexible approach be implemented first? The matter was submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau for review.

Now, we have received Instruction No. 2899 from the Social Affairs Bureau on the 5th of this month, stating that, 'The association submitted a case requesting instructions on whether the withdrawal of association members could be resolved by the executive committee first and then submitted to the general meeting for retroactive approval. We have forwarded the case and made the following instructions: We have received Consultation No. 13066 from the Municipal Government's Bureau of Industry and Commerce, stating that there are no other restrictions on the withdrawal of members from the industry trade association except that Article 5 of this law stipulates that it should be stated in the constitution. As for ceasing business or changing industries, which results in the elimination of qualifications, the membership is naturally lost even without the approval of the general membership meeting. It is permissible to ratify it at the next general membership meeting. We hereby order you to inform them.'

Therefore, it is appropriate to order the association to inform them. Upon arrival at the meeting, it was found that the stipulation that membership withdrawal must be resolved by the general membership meeting was similar to this in the constitutions of various industry trade associations in the city. Therefore, the difficult situation mentioned by the Silk Trade Association is not unique to that industry. Due to the urgent nature of the order, we are hereby issuing a letter to notify various trade associations to comply, and at the same time, we will wait until the next general membership meeting to amend Article 7 of the constitution in accordance with the Ministry's instructions."

Japan Promotes the Advantages of Japanese Silk 210

The Silk Trade Association Raises 500,000 Yuan for Promotion Expenses

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau's Silk Inspection Office of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce recently received reliable information that the Japanese Silk Association has noted that American women's purchases of silk fabrics have gradually trended towards artificial silk fabrics. This is due to the low price of artificial silk and the powerful promotional efforts. The association has passed a resolution to collect one Japanese yen for each export of raw silk, which can generate 500,000 yuan annually to promote the advantages of Japanese silk. According to Director Miao Zhongxiu, the plan was initially launched by Mr. Sant, the secretary of the Heineman Spinning Mill in Chicago, USA, who plans to hold silk exhibitions in various cities and towns in the United States to promote the advantages of natural silk in various ways, and to distinguish between natural silk and artificial silk, so that the public can choose correctly. This move is a major competition between natural silk and artificial silk, and silk-producing countries around the world should join together.

Postal Administration Received Two Orders from the Ministry of Communications 211

Cancellation of Rice Subsidies for Postal Workers

Switch to Domestically Produced Mailbags

Yesterday, the Postal Administration of this Ministry received two important orders from the Ministry of Communications, which are hereby recorded separately:

Cancellation of Rice Subsidies for Postal Workers: Order received regarding the case. It has been found that due to the high price of rice in Shanghai in the past, this Ministry, recognizing the difficulties in the lives of low-level postal workers, had issued instructions to subsidize the rice prices for these employees. However, this was a temporary measure and not a permanent one. Now that the price of rice in Shanghai has plummeted, this rice subsidy for low-level employees should be revoked to save national currency. The Postal Administration is hereby ordered to comply immediately and instruct its subordinates to be informed. This order is to be strictly followed.

Switch to Domestically Produced Mailbags: It has been found that each postal district requires the purchase of over fifty to sixty thousand canvas mailbags annually. However, the materials for these mailbags have traditionally been purchased from foreign countries, which is not only more expensive than domestic products but also results in a staggering amount of Chinese money flowing abroad each year. At a time when promoting domestic goods is encouraged, these mailbags should be switched to domestically produced materials. Domestically produced canvas is durable, resistant to water penetration, and suitable for making these mailbags. Therefore, the Postal Administration is hereby ordered that, starting this year, all mailbags purchased in the future must be made of domestically produced canvas and that foreign goods must no longer be used to prevent financial leakage and to demonstrate the promotion of domestic products. This order is to be strictly followed.

Workers at the Yingchang Factory Demand Severance Pay 212

The merger of the Yingchang Match Factory in Pudong Lujiazui with the Dachunghua Match Company has sparked a backlash from all workers, who have specifically demanded severance pay from the company that each worker is legally entitled to upon leaving the Yingchang Factory. Negotiations have been ongoing for some time, and although the Social Affairs Bureau mediated, the company requested arbitration from the Municipal Government. The outcome, rejecting the workers' demands, was decided and delivered to both labor and management the day before yesterday for compliance. After receiving the decision, the Yingchang Match Workers' Union immediately issued a notice to the workers, stating briefly: "Now that the severance pay issue has been decided by the Municipal Government, we hope that all workers will remain calm and continue working. Obey the government's orders and avoid making unnecessary moves." However, upon seeing the notice, the workers expressed dissatisfaction at not achieving their goals. The Municipal Government's arbitration decision is transcribed below: (Main text) The request by the labor side to issue severance pay is rejected. (Reason) According to the regulations, severance pay is provided to treat retiring employees with consideration. Article 1 of the Provisional Measures for Employee Severance Pay states that the regulations apply when employers in industry and commerce terminate employment relationships with employees. If there is no termination of employment between labor and management, the issue of severance pay will not arise. In this case, the labor representative claimed that the Yingchang Factory had been operating for nineteen years, the factory's capital had increased year by year, and the scope of business had expanded successively. The workers had made efforts during this time and had contributed labor. Now that the factory has closed and been merged, with the managers of the Dachunghua Company replacing the factory director and manager, the workers' side should also come to an end. Therefore, they requested the company to issue severance pay. The company representative stated that the Dachunghua Match Company merged with the Yingchang Factory, inheriting all rights and obligations of Yingchang. The company had already announced that the employment contracts and treatment conditions for the original workers of Yingchang Factory would continue to be valid. Although the company underwent restructuring, the labor side was not affected in any way. In terms of severance pay, whether or not it should be issued depends on whether there is a dismissal. Currently, the company has not dismissed anyone, and the workers have not requested dismissal. They only claim that because it is the end of the Yingchang factory, the employees have the right to enjoy severance pay in advance, which is not legally justified, and the company finds it difficult to comply with this request. After reviewing the statements from both sides, although the name of the Yingchang Match Factory has been eliminated due to the merger, the Dachunghua Company should inherit all obligations of the factory. In other words, all rights that the workers had under their contracts with the Yingchang Factory still exist as before, and their years of service will not be lost due to the company's merger, thus affecting the amount of legal severance pay they will receive in the future. Therefore, the request for severance pay for the Yingchang workers who have not been dismissed at present is not justified. Furthermore, after reviewing the regulations listed in the Measures for Employee Severance Pay, items 2, 3, and 2 state that severance pay must be issued when an employee is dismissed due to old age or disability; item 6 states that severance pay must be issued when the employer reduces the scope of employment or changes the business direction; and item 8 states that severance pay should be given based on financial resources when the employer ceases operations and dismisses employees. Although the circumstances for granting severance pay vary, the separation of the employment relationship is consistent with the actual facts of this case. The request to issue severance pay should be rejected according to law. After unanimous deliberation by all committee members, a decision is made as per the main text (omitted below).

Second Chrysanthemum Exhibition Opens at the Social Affairs Bureau Garden 224

Lunch Gathering on the Ninth

The flower show at the Municipal Garden has been fully prepared and opened for viewing today. This year, more chrysanthemums have been planted in the park than last year, with a total of more than 6,000 pots. In addition to the original varieties, this year, new species have been exchanged, collected, sorted, and analyzed from famous gardens in the capital, Yangzhou, Suzhou, and Hangzhou, totaling 267 varieties. No fewer than three to four hundred species have been contributed by all sectors. Famous gardens in this city, such as the Huang family's breeding farm, Sanyou Industrial Society, Xiaoguan Garden, Shen Xingyuan, Public School Garden, Guansheng Agricultural Farm, China Products Garden, Lu Yongmao Garden, Jiazi School Garden, Bansong Garden, Yongchun Garden, Jinan University, Labor University, and members of the Horticultural Tree Trade Association, have all selected and displayed their famous species and unseen new species, which can be called the grandest exhibition of the time. Wang Buxian's Two Sons Were Both Kidnapped

Wang Buxian, the head of Ruifengsha Township outside Wusongkou, and his son were previously kidnapped by Jiang Xingsha, the leader of the water police squad stationed near the sandbar, and Chen Guoliang, the squad leader of the 17th team of the 4th district of the Wusong water police, who were colluding with bandits. Wang took advantage of the opportunity to escape, while his son was held for ransom by the bandits for 1,500 yuan. It was reported in this newspaper that Wang's youngest son, Yulin, is still in the bandit's den and has not been released. He has already sent someone to try to rescue them.

Wang and Kang Sentenced in Scandalous Intercourse Case

The Reporting Mother and Son Blamed Each Other

Common Illegal Restriction of Personal Liberty

Threatening Extortion Attempted and Other Crimes

Wang Sentenced to Three Months, Kang to Two Months

In the case of Luo Wang's daughter, Yuying (also known as Lin Mei), a Ningbo woman from 511 Yuanjili, Tangshan Road, who is in her early twenties and has been promised in marriage to someone, Yuying suddenly had a relationship with Tang Yueqing, who lived at 412 Broadway Road. On August 17, Yuying secretly fled with her mother. Her mother and brother, Yuqing, found Yuying and Yueqing at the Suzhou Hotel on Zhejiang Road on the evening of the 21st of last month and were preparing to order them to return home when Wang Zhuqing, claiming to be a detective from the 49th branch of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, and his partner, Kang Jiabing, gathered many hooligans and took Tang Yueqing, Luo Yuying, and others to two rooms, numbers 23 and 39, at the Nanjing Hotel in the French Concession, where they were held incommunicado overnight, intending to extort 700 yuan. The case was logged in this paper. Yesterday morning, the case was re-examined in the first criminal court by Court President Xu Jiashi and Prosecutor Xu Mei of the Special Court, with the first to be summoned being Luo Yuqing, who stood in the witness box. The prosecutor's lawyer, Ru Bao-yi, said to him that after investigating the previous testimony of your confession, there were many inconsistencies with the facts, so today you must state the real language truthfully. Court President Xu then asked Luo when he reported to the Public Security Bureau after your sister disappeared. He replied that it was his mother who reported. The lawyer asked that his mother said that he made the report. The lawyer replied that he made the report to the patrol room, and his mother reported to the Public Security Bureau. The lawyer asked who Wang Yunqing and Wang A'mao were. He replied that he did not know the two people. The lawyer asked him why he said in his previous testimony that the room in Nanjing Hotel was opened by his friend. It has been found that the room was opened by the two Wangs, which is obviously inconsistent. He replied that the room was actually opened by Tang Yueqing's friend. He was asked whether he could change the testimony today. He replied that the room was actually opened by Tang's friend, and he asked that it be changed on the record. He was asked who Wang Zhuqing was and ordered him to come out. He replied that he did not know. He was asked how many people were guarding Tang Yueqing. He replied that no one was guarding him. He was asked if Wang Zhuqing was called by him. He said no. Most of the rest of the testimony contradicted the testimony given during the previous court hearing. Then, according to Tang Yueqing's testimony, the Nanjing Hotel was not opened by my friend but by Wang Zhuqing and Luo Yuqing, and Wang Zhuqing said the words "one thousand yuan" to me, and he said that he would have at least 700 yuan to settle the matter. Xu then summoned Luo Yuying to the case to ask her what she had said the last time. They first needed 1,000 yuan, but after asking for it, it was reduced to 700 yuan. According to the reply, she could not recognize who she was asking for help at the time because there were so many people, but she heard them say that if they got the money, they would have double hats (ie, 20% commission) to take. Lawyer Ru Bao-yi immediately requested that the report form submitted by the plaintiff to the Public Security Bureau be issued, and then asked the detective Qiu Si-jiu where this form came from. He replied that it was brought by the defendant Wang Zhuqing and another detective. Then he asked Luo Yuqing whether her sister needed a marriage gift to marry Tang. He replied that Tang was willing to pay 700 yuan, with 300 yuan to settle the matter with Yuying's former fiance's family and 400 yuan as a bride price. The lawyer Ru asked Tang Yueqing if he completely denied the points of Luo Yuqing's testimony, and he also asked Wang Zhuqing where the report paper came from. He replied that the plaintiff sent it to the Public Security Bureau, and he asked if it was a forgery. If this happened, please deal with it according to the law, etc. At this point, the court ordered the debate to begin. The lawyer Ru said that the testimonies of the plaintiff Luo Wang and her son Luo Yuqing contradicted each other. In other words, on the point of reporting to the Public Security Bureau, the mother pushed her son to report, and the son pushed his mother to report. In fact, neither of them had reported. Moreover, the plaintiff Luo Wang lived in the concession, and her daughter also ran away in the concession. Anyone living in the concession must know that he must report to the patrol room. The plaintiff abandoned the near and took the far, but went to report to the Public Security Bureau. There is no such foolish person in the world. From this point of view, it can be seen that the plaintiff did not actually report to the bureau, then where did this report form come from? It must be that the defendant Wang Zhuqing saw that the matter had been defeated, so he tried to forge it. If the forgery is true, then the defendant's claim that he was ordered by his superiors to investigate this case is also fabricated. Even if what he said is true, when Luo and others were found in the Suzhou Hotel, why didn't he report to the patrol room by phone and ask for help, but instead took the plaintiff to the Nanjing Hotel in the French Concession? Didn't Wang Zhuqing know the public affairs procedures? According to this lawyer's speculation, his changing hotels was indeed for criminal purposes. The Patrol Room is now accusing the two defendants of threatening extortion and obstructing freedom, and they should be severely punished. Under the vigorous defense of the defendant's lawyer Fan Gang, Court President Xu then announced in court that Wang Zhuqing had illegally restricted other people's freedom and attempted extortion, and was sentenced to three months of fixed-term imprisonment, and Kang Jiabing was sentenced to two months of fixed-term imprisonment for the same crime. The number of days of detention was converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days.

The Grand Champagne Two-Prize Winner 225

Dalian or Liaoning

Bandits Lurking Around Dianshan Lake

Merchant Ships Frequently Robbed 230

Recently, large gangs of bandits have been appearing and disappearing unpredictably in the Dianshan Lake and Yangcheng Lake area bordering Kunshan and Changshu. Merchant ships are frequently robbed when passing through. According to someone from Changshu, on the evening of the 3rd of this month, at about 8:00 PM, Wang A'gen, a firewood boat from Dongxiang, Changshu, came to Shanghai to sell firewood. While returning home empty, they were suddenly stopped by two bandit boats while passing by Dianshan Lake. Seven or eight bandits, wielding sharp blades, rushed onto the boat and immediately searched it, robbing twenty-three yuan in cash and a newly purchased package of factory cloth.

Before leaving, they also severely beat Wang A'gen several times before leaving with a whoop. Wang suffered minor head injuries and was slightly frightened, causing him to develop a fever after returning home and be bedridden.

Counterfeit Coin Manufacturing Den Uncovered on Lujiabang Road 231

Police Officers No. 216 (Western) and No. 2611 (Chinese) from the French Concession Patrol Division were patrolling North Henan Road at around 10:00 AM the day before yesterday when they saw a man acting suspiciously. They stopped him and found two hundred lead double-hao coins on his body and took him to the police station. After questioning by the police chief, he revealed his name as Lin A'er, from Fujian, and confessed that the counterfeit coin manufacturing den was located inside No. 15 Wuying Lane, Lujiabang Road, Ximen. Therefore, they dispatched Chinese Detective Shang Wu, Detective Bao Yonglu, and Western Detective Ge Sa, along with detectives from the Second District Public Security Bureau, to secretly raid the address. They seized five lead yuan, six lead jiao, as well as manufacturing equipment such as batteries, plaster powder, and lead wire mesh, and brought them back to the police station. Yesterday morning, they were handed over to the Second Criminal Court of the Special District Local Court. Wang Yao Dang, the police lawyer, presented the case and requested a postponement. The Chinese and Western detectives also reported on the situation of the raid. The seized items were submitted to the court. The defendant, Lin A'er, confessed that the counterfeit coins were made by a Zhang who is currently on the run. Yesterday, Zhang gave him two hundred counterfeit jiao to deliver to Xie Sanduo at the Laohu Stove on Shanxi Road, and he received four jiao in return. Judge Sun Yuan reviewed the confession and ordered Lin to be detained for seven days for further interrogation.

Extension of Daytime Electricity Supply in Jiajiajiao, Pudong 233

Since the Pudong Electric Company started providing daytime electricity, general users have found it convenient. However, Jiajiajiao, located between Shiba Jian and Yangjing Town, is in a remote area with very little electricity consumption, and daytime electricity has not yet been connected. Recently, businesses such as Jia Sentai and Jia Ruitai in the area felt unfairly treated for not having access to daytime electricity and filed a complaint through the Fifth District Party Headquarters to the Municipal Public Works Bureau for handling. The bureau ordered the company to provide daytime electricity to the area or to advance the current evening electricity supply time and extend it to meet the needs. It is now learned that the company believes there is no need to provide daytime electricity in the area and has complied by advancing the turn-on time of the time switches installed in the area and delaying the power outage in the morning.

Reorganization of the Huxi Defense Corps 234

The original 13th Branch of the Huxi Fahua District Defense Corps had six sub-teams: one team in Fahua Town, one team in Qianjia Lane, one team in Panjia Ku, one team in Wujia Jiao, one team in Caojiadu, and one team in Xujiahui. The number of members in each team varied, and the number of firearms in each team was also lacking and insufficient for use. Among the teams, the Caojiadu and Xujiahui teams performed the best. Now that the Defense Corps Reorganization Committee has been established, it has ordered the defense corps in each district to be reorganized, stipulating that each corps be reorganized into three teams, each with 108 members, one team leader and two deputy team leaders. The Huxi area should still be organized into one corps, with one team established in Fahua Township, one team established in Xujiahui, and one team established in Caojiadu. Since receiving the order, the corps has been reorganized. It was originally intended to complete the reorganization as soon as possible, but it was delayed due to insufficient manpower in Fahua Township. However, Caojiadu and Xujiahui have filled their quotas. Now that each district has been reorganized and winter defense is imminent, it is necessary to start immediately and reorganize and establish the corps immediately. Therefore, each team is currently engaged in merging and supplementing, and it is expected that it will be officially established soon.
